  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_87177d09-6144-41e7-9e89-84900f25914c'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3596021437167388986">It's a classic plot: a marriage of convenience that lays the groundwork for true love. <br/><br/>1119. Journeying from England to Scotland to wed a highlander, Lady Brenna had resigned herself to the arranged match. But when a band of fierce, painted warriors captured her en route, she fearlessly met their demand to marry their leader -- the quick-tempered laird Connor MacAlister. S</span>
  <span id="freeText3596021437167388986" style="display:none">It's a classic plot: a marriage of convenience that lays the groundwork for true love. <br /><br />1119. Journeying from England to Scotland to wed a highlander, Lady Brenna had resigned herself to the arranged match. But when a band of fierce, painted warriors captured her en route, she fearlessly met their demand to marry their leader -- the quick-tempered laird Connor MacAlister. She couldn't know that her capture was merely the first act of vengeance against her betrothed, Connor's sworn enemy.<br /><br />Brenna harbored no illusions that her husband was in love with her; after a hasty forest wedding, MacAlister assured her she could return home once she had borne him a son. But she could not deny that she had once proposed to MacAlister -- ten years ago, when she was just a child, and the visitor to her father's castle charmed her with his dazzling, unexpected smile. Now, as she sets out to win the brave chieftain whom she has come to adore, a legacy of revenge ensnares Brenna in a furious clan war -- and only her faith in her gallant hero can save her....</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4425363880459275996">Sheesh, it sucked to be a woman back in these days. I know, I say that a lot. She'll never see her family again, has no idea what to expect, and is sent on horseback to journey hundreds of miles to get to the guy.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303053.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>Ha!   <span id="freeText4425363880459275996" style="display:none">Sheesh, it sucked to be a woman back in these days. I know, I say that a lot. But, <b>it really <i>really</i> sucked to be a woman back then.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303050.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First, her father basically sells her to be married to some asshole they've never met and the father only tells her hours before she is sent to her new husband that this will happen. She'll never see her family again, has no idea what to expect, and is sent on horseback to journey hundreds of miles to get to the guy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303053.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Ha! She should be so lucky as to have it this easy!</i><br><br>Then, she gets kidnapped by the prospective groom's enemy and forced to marry him instead. She has to agree to marry him or else he will kill all of her father's soldiers that are with her.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303054.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>I'd rather have a gun..</i><br><br>Then, this stranger/kidnapper decides that they will consummate their wedding vows on the dirty ground in the middle of their camp, surrounded by his men. Yes, she will lose her virginity to a filthy guy who forced her to marry him in the most demeaning way possible.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303049._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Or, after being terrorized, kidnapped, and forced to ride on horseback for hours on end... either way..</i> <br><br>After losing her virginity the night before, she is expected to ride a horse for the entirety of the following day until her horse can no longer go on, at which time her new husband decides to abandon her horse. Her beloved pet is left in the woods to fend for itself. (this doesn't end well)<br><br>He also decides to abandon her belongings because they were too much trouble to carry.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303048.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>That's good, because your needs were back in that suitcase we tossed because it was too heavy.</i><br><br>Finally, when he gets her to her new home - a fortress - he takes off for a couple of weeks, leaving her in an unfamiliar country, with no friends or family, barely knowing the language.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303052.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Welcome to your new life!</i><br><br>The worst part of all this? It was normal crap for back then. Women were simply servant/baby makers. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490334932i/22303051._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Don't forget to make him a sandwich when you are done.</i><br><br>Can we all just get down on our knees and thank God that we were born in this era?<br><br>Still, the story in this book was cute and funny. Even though women had no rights or the ability to resist what was being done to them, I like that our heroine still found ways to manipulate <s>her overlords</s> the men around her. She was clever and sweet. The man, however, was an ass until the very end.</span>

<div id="review_45263990" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45263990" />
    <a title="Dina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1918270-dina"><img alt="Dina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1460302951p2/1918270.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/45263990?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dina" href="/user/show/1918270-dina">Dina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1918270-dina?shelf=to-blog">to-blog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer45263990" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14235315749383310465">So it happened... I found a book by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6251.Julie_Garwood' title='Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>Julie Garwood</a> that I didn't love. Not that it was bad, it was just not up to par with the other Garwood books I've read.<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107778.The_Wedding__Lairds__Fianc_es___2_' title='The Wedding (Lairds' Fiancées, #2) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wedding</a> starts with 10-year-old Highlander Connor MacAlister promising his dying father to avenge his death by finding out and killing the ones who betrayed him. This promise basically defines Connor's whole life then and determines the course of his actions throughout the story. 16 years later, Connor's quest for revenge makes him steal </span>
  <span id="freeText14235315749383310465" style="display:none">So it happened... I found a book by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/6251.Julie_Garwood" title="Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">Julie Garwood</a> that I didn't love. Not that it was bad, it was just not up to par with the other Garwood books I've read.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107778.The_Wedding__Lairds__Fianc_es___2_" title="The Wedding (Lairds' Fiancées, #2) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wedding</a> starts with 10-year-old Highlander Connor MacAlister promising his dying father to avenge his death by finding out and killing the ones who betrayed him. This promise basically defines Connor's whole life then and determines the course of his actions throughout the story. 16 years later, Connor's quest for revenge makes him steal away his enemy's bride, Lady Brenna, an Englishwoman who he met some years ago when he was a young lad and she was a child, and who innocently proposed to him back then. Connor isn't aware that Brenna is his enemy's bride when he sets out to claim her as his own bride, but he's more than satisfied now that he knows it.<br /><br />What follows is one of the funniest wedding scenes I've ever read. It wasn't as good as the one in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107776.Ransom__Highlands__Lairds___2_" title="Ransom (Highlands' Lairds, #2) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">Ransom</a>, but it was a blast and I giggled all the way through it. After they're properly married, Connor and Brenna start their journey back to his home, where he can drop her and keep working on his revenge against his father's killers. And that's where the story lost me...<br /><br />I really enjoyed the 1st half of the book, and I could have bet it was going to be another winner to me. I was definitely starting to fall for Connor, the arrogant and gruff warrior who had - or seemed to have - a soft spot when it came to his new wife, even if he would have killed himself before he acknowledged it. I adored Brenna, the somewhat clueless young lady who was decided to make the best of a bad situation while trying to find a way out of it. And I loved Garwood's humorous writing, that had me smiling and laughing at the nonsense that came out of Connor's mouth and mind. I knew - or better, hoped - his cold and bossy behavior would start to change a bit as he got to spend more time with Brenna and build a true relationship with her, so I put up with him in the beginning. Unfortunately, that change never came...<br /><br />I swear, I started to frown when Connor left Brenna to her own devices as soon as he arrived home, <i>trusting</i> her to follow him around. WTH, did he think she was like a pet? And when he "found" her - not that he'd ever admit he had "lost" her in the 1st place! -, he didn't appologize for having forgotten about her. No, he berated her for the grievance she'd put him through. What a charming man. Not!<br /><br />Then, things got worse when Connor just up and went to fight some battle against one of his enemies next, leaving his newlywed wife Brenna to deal with his stepmother and his stepbrother alone. At that point, everything went down hill. Brenna, who I still liked by then, started to act like an idiot, failing to see what a b!tch Connor's stepmother was. <i>Anyone</i>, including the servants, could see that, but Brenna kept illuding herself into thinking the old woman was just "difficult". Naturally, no good came from Brenna's willingness to hide from the truth right before her eyes. She pretty much became a pushover, and that was so different from how she'd behaved in the 1st half of the story that I started to wonder if I was reading the same book.<br /><br />As I finished the book, I was still trying to figure out why and how exactly Connor and Brenna fell in love with each other. They didn't <i>know</i> each other at all and kept misunderstanding their feelings and actions. Connor's constant refusal to talk and explain himself - he was Laird, why should he "waste" his time explaining his actions to his wife? - didn't help matters. He was so focused on avenging his father's death that I never felt he dedicated enough time to actually fall for Brenna. Okay, he was all mushy and head-over-hills in love with her by the end of the book, but I had a hard time buying it. I mean, this was the same man who'd left her alone at home right after their hasty wedding, wasn't it? As for Brenna, I also didn't understand why she fell for Connor considering how he'd basically neglected her most of the time and hadn't shown any glimpse of loving affection before the final pages.<br /><br />All things considered, this was kind of a disappointing read. Like I said, it wasn't bad, but I had high expectations - which were reinfoced by the wonderful 1st half of the story - and they weren't met. But I don't regret reading it and I'm going to keep it, as I may feel in the mood to reread the 1st half in the future.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14235315749383310465" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3477082759" />
    <a title="EmBibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62566585-embibliophile"><img alt="EmBibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551380716p2/62566585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3477082759?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="EmBibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="EmBibliophile" href="/user/show/62566585-embibliophile">EmBibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3477082759" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10067953492805792411"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I wasn’t a huge fan of this one or I guess my historical romance fever has finally been broken and I’m now ready to go back to the 21st century books.<br/><br/>The heroine was just a pushover and I prefer my HR heroines to be sassy and spirited. This one annoyed the hell out of me. I didn’t like the hero at all. He’s so freakin obtuse. I kept hoping for a change in his personality but it never came. I also couldn’t feel any chemistry between the heroine and the hero. I couldn’t see how they love </span>
  <span id="freeText10067953492805792411" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />I wasn’t a huge fan of this one or I guess my historical romance fever has finally been broken and I’m now ready to go back to the 21st century books.<br /><br />The heroine was just a pushover and I prefer my HR heroines to be sassy and spirited. This one annoyed the hell out of me. I didn’t like the hero at all. He’s so freakin obtuse. I kept hoping for a change in his personality but it never came. I also couldn’t feel any chemistry between the heroine and the hero. I couldn’t see how they love each other. It didn’t feel like they even get to know each other. I don’t think that there was a single scene where I felt any connection between them. Most scenes ended with some kind of degradation or a really hurtful comment that got me raging. The writing is really good tho and I loved the wedding scene but that’s it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10067953492805792411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_36569719" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/36569719" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/36569719?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of medieval historical scottish romance, and exceptional heroines</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=scottish">scottish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=sweet-heroine">sweet-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=captive-kidnapped">captive-kidnapped</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=angsty-read">angsty-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=laughed-myself-silly-while-reading">laughed-myself-silly-while-reading</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=revenge">revenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=heroine-i-adore">heroine-i-adore</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer36569719" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1982236660288434265">The Wedding managed to make its way up into the ranks of Garwood books that earned a five star rating. Why? Because this book took me from laughing hysterically, to being angry enough for my blood pressure to shoot up (or so my throbbing temples testified to), to being so sad I wanted to cry. Also, it's just darn entertaining.<br/><br/>I've read many, many romance novels in my thirty-some years, and Julie Garwood has a way of writing singular heroines, like no other author. On first glance, they seem too </span>
  <span id="freeText1982236660288434265" style="display:none">The Wedding managed to make its way up into the ranks of Garwood books that earned a five star rating. Why? Because this book took me from laughing hysterically, to being angry enough for my blood pressure to shoot up (or so my throbbing temples testified to), to being so sad I wanted to cry. Also, it's just darn entertaining.<br /><br />I've read many, many romance novels in my thirty-some years, and Julie Garwood has a way of writing singular heroines, like no other author. On first glance, they seem too sweet to be believed. But, their sweetness is completely genuine. Her heroines are so kind and loving, that you'd have to be a big jerk to hate them. As for me, I love them. Brenna certainly was no different. The poor girl. She really went through the wringer in this book, and Connor contributed significantly to her suffering. At times, I did want to take a frying pan to his thick skull. Of course, I realize that he's emotionally stunted from the tragedy of his father's betrayal and death, and the murder of most of his clan. His deathbed promise to his father was what drove him, and marriage was only a secondary concern. He's a hard man, and it took him sometime to realize that his husband skills needed improvement. You cannot put wives away on shelves to gather dust until you want to play with them, man! Thankfully, love conquers all. <br /><br />This was a very good book, and I didn't want to put it down. Brenna won my heart, and I was very glad that Connor got a clue. I loved the secondary cast of characters, such as Connor's men Quinlan and Crispin, and his people, Father Sinclair, her family, and of course, Laird Alec and Lady Jamie. I'm not sure if medieval Scotland in any way resembles this book, but I almost want to go there just to enjoy the ambience (despite the lack of indoor plumbing). <br /><br /> I don't have it in me to write a long review right now, so this will have to suffice. How does Ms. Garwood do it? Write such brilliant comedy, but scenes that are ripe with emotional anguish? Those diametrically opposed tones shouldn't go together, but she manages it. Although some parts wrenched at my heart at what poor Brenna went through, I felt that things worked out very well. I know that Connor will never, ever take her for granted again. He'll realize just how precious the love he has with Brenna, and how that was more important than the vengeance his father swore him to. She snuck her way into his heart, just like she did mine.<br /><br />Darn! I wish I had time to go back and read all her historicals again!</span>
  <a data-text-id="1982236660288434265" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

One of the hardest categories for me...I shall admit it. </b><br/><br/><b>Series:</b> I believe it is. <br/><br/><b>Sexy times:</b> Meh. <br/><br/><b>Plan on reading more by the author: </b>At times I consider it.   <span id="freeText9110507785847488034" style="display:none"><b>Deliver me from witless heroines and ignorant heroes. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1497411236ra/23020266.gif" width="320" height="240" alt="shaking" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Considering this a bodice ripper for my Year Long Historical Romance Challenge. One of the hardest categories for me...I shall admit it. </b><br><br><b>Series:</b> I believe it is. <br><br><b>Sexy times:</b> Meh. <br><br><b>Plan on reading more by the author: </b>At times I consider it. Well no, I shall not. Should I tell him his stepmother is undermining me at every turn. Nah. Can I see reality when it slaps me upside the head? No. She has moments of fun and smarts but these are overshadowed by her desire to win a Darwin award. <br><br><b>Hero:</b> Connor. Good lord here as well. I can see my new wife is upset, but she can take care of whatever it is. It's just females figuring their figurative shit out. She doesn't need to know. Alright already. We get it. You're an ass. <br><br><b>Why it did or didn't work for me:</b> <br>So long. So so so long. The same thing. Nothing new really happened. She's dim, he's an ass. Bored. I got nothing for you. Sorry. I just can't muster the energy one way or the other. It's not worth my rant. <br><br>Signed, <br><b>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=book-everyone-loved-but-me">book-everyone-loved-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=cruel-hero">cruel-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=obstinate-annoying-heroine">obstinate-annoying-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=what-does-she-see-in-him">what-does-she-see-in-him</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175401846" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17739671651534102088"><b>2 stars</b><br/><br/>Looks like I'm one of the few who didn't enjoy this book. I had high hopes to start but ended up disappointed and frustrated for most of the books.<br/><br/>I found "The Wedding" frustrating, wearisome, and confusing at times. There were some funny and endearing parts, but those moments soon gave way to frustration again. I also had a devil of a time trying to connecting with these characters. I didn't hate the book but I certainly didn't like it either.<br/><br/>I'm not sure why this story didn't sit well w</span>
  <span id="freeText17739671651534102088" style="display:none"><b>2 stars</b><br /><br />Looks like I'm one of the few who didn't enjoy this book. I had high hopes to start but ended up disappointed and frustrated for most of the books.<br /><br />I found "The Wedding" frustrating, wearisome, and confusing at times. There were some funny and endearing parts, but those moments soon gave way to frustration again. I also had a devil of a time trying to connecting with these characters. I didn't hate the book but I certainly didn't like it either.<br /><br />I'm not sure why this story didn't sit well with me. I guess after reading "The Bride," a book with characters that jumped off the pages and had such heart &amp; soul, "The Wedding" felt tedious and slightly obnoxious. The constant misconceptions between the two main characters became annoying after awhile. And, for heaven's sake, could Connor become any more obtuse?<br /><br />I felt Brenna and Connor had little, if any, character growth throughout the book, although Connor did change his feelings about marriage and Brenna toward the end. Brenna's character, on the other hand, seemed to retrogress. She began as a feisty, confident, and witty women; only to become a weak reflection of her former self. It was sad watching such a vibrant and carefree character become more and more passiveness as the story progressed. In her desire to be accepted by her mother-in-law, which she believed would have a positive impact on her relationship with Connor, she allowed herself to become easily controlled and manipulated. Thankfully, she rectified that mentality by the end of the book.<br /><br />Connor is definitely my least favorite alpha-hero. He's 100% alpha-male, with hardly a redeeming quality throughout the book. He's one of the most cantankerous, egomaniac, obtuse characters I've read. Good grief, the guy’s about as clueless as they come with regard to women. I didn't find him at all endearing. He did redeem himself at the end; however, it felt like the author forced his character into submission. Because his change of heart was not a natural progression, it seemed abrupt, and there for, not totally believable. <br /><br />For me, Connor’s and Brenna's relationship was the most disconcerting aspect of the book. Frankly, I couldn’t find any reason to root for them as a couple. Connor was constantly rebuking, disregarding, berating, and patronizing Brenna. Also, Connor said one of the cruelest things a man could say to a woman in regard to her worth as a wife. I had a difficult time forgiving him for that.<br /><br />How on earth these two fell in love is beyond me. They definitely had great chemistry between the sheets (Julie Garwood can write some steamy smexin, that's for sure) but that's the only time I really felt the chemistry between them. Not only were they constantly bickering, they spent very little time together during the second half of the book. Honestly, their love story baffled me.<br /><br />There were some funny and heartwarming parts I did like.<br /><br />The wedding scene was brilliantly written. I can't help but laugh just thinking about it. Julie Garwood sure has a knack for writing humor.<br /><br />I teared up when Brenna gave Connor the medallion she'd made him, explaining the reason why it was so dear to her. The way she compared the story of David and Goliath to Connor's history was beautiful and heartwarming. It was the only time I felt a deep connection between the two of them. <br /><br />I really loved that Alec and Jamie (The Bride) made a few appearances in this book. I absolutely love their characters. Their little three year old daughter was so darling and fun; she stole the show whenever she made an appearance in the book.<br /><br /> Honestly, I think my expectations for this book were a tad too high after just finishing "The Bride.” I can’t help but make comparisons between the two and, frankly, “The Wedding” falls short!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17739671651534102088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText1157079787461253615" style="display:none">I really loved The Bride and was really disappointed by The Wedding. 2.5 stars<br /><br />The book gets 2.5 stars because :<br /><br />1 Brenna tried to be clever to get her way. I say tried, because it didn't happen as often as I expected.<br /><br />2 The scene with the wedding vows. I hope the book had more banter and a defiant Brenna.<br /><br />“She will honor me, protect me, obey me only when she believes I’m being reasonable—but I shouldn’t hold out hope that that day will ever come—try to love me before she’s an old woman, and I’d better get it straight in my mind that she will respect me until or unless I do something to prove I’m not worthy, and God save me then. Have I left anything out, Brenna?” <br />“Nay, Connor,” she answered. “You made better sense out of my vows than I did.” <br /><br />Half Star - Connor is clueless but tries to keep Brenna happy and comfortable.<br />“I cannot guess what you want. <div id="review_103515031" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103515031" />
    <a title="Crista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3194546-crista"><img alt="Crista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1284946251p2/3194546.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103515031?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Crista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Crista" href="/user/show/3194546-crista">Crista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=lol">lol</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3194546-crista?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103515031" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13796342013749341332">The Bride followed by The Wedding are, in my opinion, Garwood's best work. If you are new to Garwood, these 2 books are a great place to start. <br/><br/>Julie Garwood is different than most of the romance authors that I read in the fact that I find myself loving her heroines even more than her heroes! I usually read romance novels for the larger than life men they ususally come with, but Garwood's Ladies steal the show. <br/><br/>In The Wedding, Brenna is one of those "show stealers". This character is so refreshi</span>
  <span id="freeText13796342013749341332" style="display:none">The Bride followed by The Wedding are, in my opinion, Garwood's best work. If you are new to Garwood, these 2 books are a great place to start. <br /><br />Julie Garwood is different than most of the romance authors that I read in the fact that I find myself loving her heroines even more than her heroes! I usually read romance novels for the larger than life men they ususally come with, but Garwood's Ladies steal the show. <br /><br />In The Wedding, Brenna is one of those "show stealers". This character is so refreshing that I wanted to name our "first born" after her! Now that is some serious writing power Ms. Garwood! <br /><br />Brenna is "quirky" but so much fun! She is beautiful, but humble. She has a large appetite for food and isn't afraid to use it. She is honest with her affections and doesn't mind giving her unapproachable husband public displays of affection. She is loyal and loving...whether it's to her horse or her husband. She isn't prideful, but tells Connor exactly how she feels in direct and clear ways. In one part of the story, Connor believes that in the "morning after" she will be so shocked at his behavior in the bedroom that "out of courtesy" he has her moved out of his bedroom. Brenna is maddened by this an confronts her intimidating husband without apology to get moved back into his bedroom. She had me laughing, shocked, and respecting her throughout the book. <br /><br />Connor is the quintessential Garwood hero. Tortured, but not overly so. Powerful, but not to much so. Attractive, and very much so! However, the real gem in this book is Brenna who holds so much power without ever knowing it or wanting it. I loved her.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13796342013749341332" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review103515031">

<span id="freeTextContainer16821773383287993148">This was a good mix of camp and serious. Definitely darker than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107779.The_Bride__Lairds__Fianc_es___1_' title='The Bride (Lairds' Fiancées, #1) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bride</a>, but still contained Garwood's wit and humor. <br/><br/>Poor Brenna goes through it and a lot of it is the hero's fault. He doesn't actually treat her cruelly himself, but he's very tied up in his vengeance plots against another Laird and leaves her to the crappy in-laws from hell. Also the enemy Laird does a terrible thing that really upset me. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[He kills her horse and has the remains sent to her and Conner. <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoi</a></span></span>

  <span id="freeText14641513326959683602" style="display:none">Another beautiful read with such emotional moments I cried and laughed so many times. I would have liked more happy times before the epilogue but it was still one of couldn't put down. Connor and Brenna had such a tug of war going on yet it just worked. He was so stubbornly ignorant that it was actually endearing to see him realize his love and that he's stronger for it not weaker. Big rough, stubborn, arrogant and egotistical alphas.. They seem to be my weakness especially and only if they are loyal and protective from the start which Connor fit perfectly. <br /><br />#SafeRead</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1553565865?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves" href="/user/show/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves">Preeti ♥︎ Her Bookshelves</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=e-highlander-scot">e-highlander-scot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=g-hx-rom">g-hx-rom</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=revenge-payback-vindicatn">revenge-payback-vindicatn</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=hero-alpha-hot">hero-alpha-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=me_made-me-swoon">me_made-me-swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=stained-sheets-n-all">stained-sheets-n-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=calm-down-girl">calm-down-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=moc-arrnged-forcd-mino">moc-arrnged-forcd-mino</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32506772-preeti-her-bookshelves?shelf=older-guy-10-yrs-or-more">older-guy-10-yrs-or-more</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1553565865" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17886169491122726907">I quite adore my highlanders. Untamed, brawny, kilted- they have this unique uber hot quality ah canna resist! And Julie Garwood does a fair job presenting them. Her ‘The bride’ was beautifully done with a surly H brought to heel by a sweet innocent and giving bride.<br/><br/>In this sequel, she does it again. The premise and tone is the same in this one and the start was very promising. I love an abducted bride and a forced marriage do, and these two have a sweet history and are not strictly strangers. A</span>
  <span id="freeText17886169491122726907" style="display:none">I quite adore my highlanders. Untamed, brawny, kilted- they have this unique uber hot quality ah canna resist! And Julie Garwood does a fair job presenting them. Her ‘The bride’ was beautifully done with a surly H brought to heel by a sweet innocent and giving bride.<br /><br />In this sequel, she does it again. The premise and tone is the same in this one and the start was very promising. I love an abducted bride and a forced marriage do, and these two have a sweet history and are not strictly strangers. As a 5-6 yrs. old, she had set her eyes on the adult H and proposed to him, which was aww so sweet and all. So when in the present, he decides to abduct his enemy’s intended and realizes it’s the brat from the past who wanted to be his bride, he takes the excuse of finally accepting her proposal. In true Julie Garwood tradition, the h is sweet, ditsy, funny and amenable. Her hs don’t create too much fuss or friction, but manage the inflexible Hs with their philosophy of honey over vinegar! The book had some real funny and delightful moments. <br /><br />But then it gets ponderous towards the end with its predictableness and nothing much else happening. The h also starts getting on your nerves with her silly antics. You can take only so much cuteness! I began thinking that as a character she’s fine, but if I had to constantly tolerate such a person in real life, I would probably throttle her and hide the body.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17886169491122726907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_139540352" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/139540352" />
    <a title="Autumn  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4261004-autumn"><img alt="Autumn  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325839567p2/4261004.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139540352?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">historical romance readers.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Autumn   by: </span>
      anja
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4261004-autumn?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4261004-autumn?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4261004-autumn?shelf=part-of-series">part-of-series</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139540352" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12649204409398506062">ohh.. It was a good read alright!! :)<br/><br/>I have to say that i favor the themes where couple is married from the start,and make it work out. It eliminates some nonsense, specially from historical. <br/><br/>This book is the second installment of the Laird series. I enjoyed the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107779.The_Bride__Lairds__Fianc_es___1_' title='The Bride (Lairds' Fiancées, #1) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bride</a>,but i felt this books was much more thorough, hence more satisfying ending.<br/><br/>I loved the way Garwood developed this characters;we had enough information on both of them from their childhood.which makes the plot a notch more deep.</span>
  <span id="freeText12649204409398506062" style="display:none">ohh.. It was a good read alright!! :)<br /><br />I have to say that i favor the themes where couple is married from the start,and make it work out. It eliminates some nonsense, specially from historical. <br /><br />This book is the second installment of the Laird series. I enjoyed the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107779.The_Bride__Lairds__Fianc_es___1_" title="The Bride (Lairds' Fiancées, #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bride</a>,but i felt this books was much more thorough, hence more satisfying ending.<br /><br />I loved the way Garwood developed this characters;we had enough information on both of them from their childhood.which makes the plot a notch more deep. Connor`s battered childhood explain so much about his lack of tactfulness. In some other book a character such as him would have made me annoyed,instead Connor had me laughing with the genuine lack of knowledge on interpreting emotions. As per Brenna, well...I liked Brenna,but i did have some issues with her.. she was fierce enough to face such an abrupt change of fate,but at the same time her insecurities made her seem like doormat. (that back and forth train of thought was the little speck in the story IMO).but she is very funny too.. so she is in my good list of heroines LOL<br /><br />The plot was AMAZING! is one of those books that you can see how much thought and care it has been put into it. Its perhaps one of the very few books where i was so enchanted with the beginning.. it was sooo adorable!! little mischief running with the piglet, and what about their first meeting in the camp?? whoa i loved it!!! <br /><br />I also had the opportunity to visit Jamie and Alec,since the bride had no epilogue. I had many good times laughing at the quips from both H/H to second characters.. you see, in this early settings is quite difficult to make a story that has humor yet remains genuine to its era. I never thought i would enjoy medieval books and this one proved me just plain wrong! <br /><br />the ending was beautiful!! the real challenge of a relationship is finding a way to work it out to an everlasting commitment. to accept,understand and be able to incorporate the shortcomings into a happily ever after! for me it cant get more real and better than that!<br /><br />ps: prologue and epilogue included in this story! thats hows done!!! </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12853249958591194816"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>These books are hit and misses with me. Overall, I did enjoy this one, but towards the end, I was getting kind of tired of the story (it’s a REALLY LONG book) and skimmed the last 20%.<br/><br/>I liked the tone and feel of this one, but it’s not my favorite. I didn’t agree with the way the Hero treated the Heroine at times and I kind of wanted a stronger Heroine.<br/><br/>But you get all the feels, you get the virgin bride that didn’t know she was getting married.   <span id="freeText12853249958591194816" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br /><br />These books are hit and misses with me. Overall, I did enjoy this one, but towards the end, I was getting kind of tired of the story (it’s a REALLY LONG book) and skimmed the last 20%.<br /><br />I liked the tone and feel of this one, but it’s not my favorite. I didn’t agree with the way the Hero treated the Heroine at times and I kind of wanted a stronger Heroine.<br /><br />But you get all the feels, you get the virgin bride that didn’t know she was getting married. You got the protector Hero and fighting highlanders. I do like there was less politics in this one.<br /><br />It was a decent read, but not my favorite. <br /></span>

<div id="review_600690022" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/600690022" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8278010-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1352109855p2/8278010.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/600690022?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/8278010-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11670493-the-wedding">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8278010-jo?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer600690022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1739030793383719238"><br/>Lady Brenna was in the Highlands because her father got her an arranged match. However on her journey, a fierce group of highlanders (painted like they were going to war),say she is going to wed her leader, Connor. <br/>Connor reminds her that she did asked him to marry her 3 times and that he is finally accepting. A bold move for a women of that time,right? Lets just say that she was a toddler when she ask him, barely not remembering that she actually did it.<br/>So in order to save her fathers soldiers,</span>
  <span id="freeText1739030793383719238" style="display:none"><br>Lady Brenna was in the Highlands because her father got her an arranged match. However on her journey, a fierce group of highlanders (painted like they were going to war),say she is going to wed her leader, Connor. <br>Connor reminds her that she did asked him to marry her 3 times and that he is finally accepting. A bold move for a women of that time,right? Lets just say that she was a toddler when she ask him, barely not remembering that she actually did it.<br>So in order to save her fathers soldiers, she agrees to marry him. And Connor wants to marry her on an act of revenge, agaist her former betrothed, the man he thinks is responsible for his father death!<br><br>But it comes a time, where the reasons they got married ceases to exist and the attraction they feel for each other threatens to overwhelm them!<br><br><a href="http://imageshack.us/photo/my-images/585/tumblrmn1lyn44yv1sr7fsp.gif/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380419170ra/830759.gif" alt="Image Hosted by ImageShack.us" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br><b>
  <i> He knew exactly why he'd needed her so much. He'd been living with rage for such a long time, and she was such a gentle,loving spirit. He'd needed her to breathe,to feel...</i>
</b><br><br><br>Seriously you guys, it seems it won't be soon that I get off this highlander stories mood. THIS IS JUST SO GOOD!!!<br><br><b> 4 stars </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="1739030793383719238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2058010572" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2628634423829033321"><b>4.5 Stars!</b><br/><br/>I love this series! The inner dialogue of these characters is hilarious. We have a great heroine who does not conform to the demure, obedient female mold of those times. A dominant highlander male who is exasperated with his wife's antics but loves, treasures and protects her above all else. Just fantastic! Still not better than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107779.The_Bride__Lairds__Fianc_es___1_' title='The Bride (Lairds' Fiancées, #1) by Julie Garwood' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bride</a> though.</span>

We have a great heroine who does not conform to the demure, obedient female mold of those times. A dominant highlander male who is exasperated with his wife's antics but loves, treasures and protects her above all else. Just fantastic! Still not better than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/107779.The_Bride__Lairds__Fianc_es___1_" title="The Bride (Lairds' Fiancées, #1) by Julie Garwood" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bride</a> though.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3233131028?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leigh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leigh" href="/user/show/5650814-leigh">Leigh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/39799191-the-wedding">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5650814-leigh?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5650814-leigh?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3233131028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5415541275146519933">The Wedding was another enjoyable read but I did enjoyed book 1 more. I found Connor and Brenna exhausting. Connor was cold and Brenna tried so hard to please him that I was frustrated for more than half of the book. The second half was a lot better but I do wish we were able to see a little more of Connor's softer side. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oraJzHyRqYoOcqSoDv4a4ZAySoLrhrd36WYfdJqy+NrMgZE9QSlsEKqv+SzAS/YzqXy30AWSh9JfUtJNaXnWvw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('k9SiHdetN2lSafn+TTVHtUjpvTjweB7onR4qZZsU7pb947rs6hXy8/a0pHqDgKtncadAah5sLk0rKudcaN/A8w==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer379529312521934277">With more than 35 million books in print and 26 NEW YORK TIMES bestsellers, Julie Garwood has earned a position among America's favorite fiction writers.<br/><br/>Born and raised in Kansas City, MO, Ms. Garwood attributes much of her success to growing up in a large family of Irish heritage. "The Irish are great storytellers who relish getting all of the details and nuances of every situation. Add in the fa</span>
  <span id="freeText379529312521934277" style="display:none">With more than 35 million books in print and 26 NEW YORK TIMES bestsellers, Julie Garwood has earned a position among America's favorite fiction writers.<br /><br />Born and raised in Kansas City, MO, Ms. Garwood attributes much of her success to growing up in a large family of Irish heritage. "The Irish are great storytellers who relish getting all of the details and nuances of every situation. Add in the fact that I was the sixth of seven children. Early in life, I learned that self expression had to be forceful, imaginative, and quick," says Ms. Garwood. <br /><br />She began her writing career when the youngest of her three children entered school. After the publications of two young-adult books, she turned her talents to historical fiction. Her first novel, GENTLE WARRIOR, was published by Pocket Books in 1985. Since then, she has branched into other genres including contemporary romantic suspense. Today, her name appears regularly on the bestseller lists of every major publication in the country, and her books are translated into dozens of languages around the world. Her bestselling novel FOR THE ROSES was adapted for the HALLMARK HALL OF FAME television movie ROSE HILL.<br /><br />Ms. Garwood lives in Leawood, KS and is currently working on her next novel.</span>

The Bride sweeps readers back to the savage beauty of medieval Scotland....  By the king\'s edict, Alec Kincaid, mightiest of the Scottish lairds, must take an English bride. And Jaime the youngest daughter of Baron Jamison, is his choice. From his first glimpse of the proud and beautiful English lady, Alec felt a burning hunger stir within him. This was a woman worthy of his fearless warrior\'s spirit. And he aches to touch her, tame her, possess her...forever.  But with the wedding vows, Jamie pledges her own secret oath: She will never surrender her love to this Highland barbarian. He was everything her heart warned her against -- an arrogant, brooding scoundrel whose rough good looks and seductive embrace fire her blood. But when strange accidents begin to threaten Jamie\'s life and an old rumor that Alec killed his first wife spreads anew, something far more dangerous than desire threatens to conquer her senses.  With all the storytelling power and insight into the human heart that have made her one of the bestselling authors of our time, Julie Garwood takes readers on an unforgettable romantic journey rich in
